<div id="review_430643883" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/430643883" />
    <a title="M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4898286-m"><img alt="M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1330647592p2/4898286.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/430643883?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="M." href="/user/show/4898286-m">M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781478322306" href="/book/show/15748898-my-favorite-mistake">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4898286-m?shelf=ya-contemporary-romance">ya-contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4898286-m?shelf=books-i-couldn-t-finish">books-i-couldn-t-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4898286-m?shelf=couldn-t-get-into-it">couldn-t-get-into-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4898286-m?shelf=books-with-stupid-annoying-heroines">books-with-stupid-annoying-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4898286-m?shelf=heroes-who-act-like-girls">heroes-who-act-like-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4898286-m?shelf=meh-hero">meh-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4898286-m?shelf=one-track-mind-heroine">one-track-mind-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4898286-m?shelf=very-cliche">very-cliche</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer430643883" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4335333114795753837"><b> REVIEW WITH SPOILERS </b><br/><br/>This book failed to impress me from chapter one but I wasn't expecting much, to be honest. My Favorite Mistake has two one dimensional characters that I failed to connect with. We got Taylor, a short tempered, evil bitch character that despite being the victim of a sexual assault failed miserably to make me feel sorry for her, mainly because she was a rude, mean person, who thought that just because she had a fucked up past she was entitled to bursts of violence against the</span>
  <span id="freeText4335333114795753837" style="display:none"><b> REVIEW WITH SPOILERS </b><br /><br />This book failed to impress me from chapter one but I wasn't expecting much, to be honest. My Favorite Mistake has two one dimensional characters that I failed to connect with. We got Taylor, a short tempered, evil bitch character that despite being the victim of a sexual assault failed miserably to make me feel sorry for her, mainly because she was a rude, mean person, who thought that just because she had a fucked up past she was entitled to bursts of violence against the opposite sex.<br />The male counterpart was supposed to be a bad boy with all his tattoos and suave moves but he was anything but that. I guess the author figured that the recipe for badasserey is a buzz cut hair and tattoos. Talk about stereotyping. Hunter was just a traumatized guy who despite having a fucked up past (more fucked up than Taylor's if you ask me) treated everyone with compassion and respect. He was just too nice and didn't deserve the way Taylor abused him verbally and physically. Note to the author: just having characters saying that Hunter was an ass didn't make him an ass. He didn't act like one and I don't think a guy making funny, harmless comments about sex makes him a douchebag.<br />The reversed double standards in this book had me almost pulling my hair out. How is it okay to have the protagonist assault her love interest on several occasions and that be normal? But when Taylor crossed the line with Hunter and he kicked her out of the apartment it was a huge deal? WTF? Chelsea, I think you are taking your feminist views a bit too far. Abuse is abuse regardless of the gender of the one on the receiving end.<br />Three quarters of the book consisted of Hunter chasing after Taylor and Taylor being a bitch to him. Taylor pretty much threatens Hunter's secret out of him but she can't return the favor and reveal hers. When she finally reveals her secret and has sex with Hunter it was like her character went through a 180 degree change but by that point I had completely lost interest in the story. <br />I can see some similarities between My Favorite Mistake and Beautiful Disaster but to be completely honest, MFM has nothing on Beautiful Disaster. That was a great book. This one was simply put a lame attempt.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4335333114795753837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7547269-pages-in-pink?shelf=reviewed-2012">reviewed-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer424746297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5960808864979990248">This book swings in with a firm three stars for moi- here is why folks:<br/><br/>Here.We.Go.<br/><br/>Taylor is beginning her Sophomore year of college at UMaine- One of her roommates has backed out last minute and a replacement sent to the dorm room she shares with Darah and Renee- all good..except... the new roomie is a DUDE! No WAY! Not only that, but a HOT dude. Woot!!! <br/><br/>She is beyond livid that she has to share ANY space with "HIM" (aka Hunter)... in addition to THAT- She drew the short straw and gets to bunk w</span>
  <span id="freeText5960808864979990248" style="display:none">This book swings in with a firm three stars for moi- here is why folks:<br /><br />Here.We.Go.<br /><br />Taylor is beginning her Sophomore year of college at UMaine- One of her roommates has backed out last minute and a replacement sent to the dorm room she shares with Darah and Renee- all good..except... the new roomie is a DUDE! No WAY! Not only that, but a HOT dude. Woot!!! <br /><br />She is beyond livid that she has to share ANY space with "HIM" (aka Hunter)... in addition to THAT- She drew the short straw and gets to bunk with him- Horrible I say!!! Bunking with a hot, tattooed sex pot- who would DO such a thing??? (GASP!!!!)<br /><br />So she blesses him with a right hook and a knee in the nuts. Surprise and welcome home! (rolling eyes)- then they go out and have drinks. Happens all the time to me. (Shaking head)<br /><br />Needless to say, she gives him the cold shoulder and blankets him in all kinds of arctic air, reveling in her old high school nickname, "Ice Queen". Despite his awesome treatment/ welcome, he gives her three options to get him to voluntarily move out: Prove you hate me, love me, or sleep with me... all while staring at her chest. JOY!<br /><br />Now. For me this book starts out down the right track- tenacious heroine- angry, a little bitter, full of sass.... badass hero just waiting to take our heroine off guard and lay down the law- that is where my praise on this topic ends. Soon, our heroine just sounds like an outright BEOTCH. Not a cute, cuddly, run away from feelings because she is scared kind of a thing- B.E.O.T.C.H. <br /><br />I found myself saying "ooohhh HELL to tha NO!!!... Tell her to kiss your ass!!! Teach her some manners!!!" It didn't matter. Hunter didn't listen to anything I said (Helllooooo?????) He just took it. Literally. A few slaps, a few more hits, a few more attempts at the family jewels. About 100 more "I.Fucking.Hate.You"'s, "Get.away.from.me"'s- this is how much of this went:<br /><br />"I'll make you a deal, Missy." (his nickname for her)<br />"Why would I want to make a deal with you?'<br />"Just hear me out. If you can prove to me that you hate me, absolutely hate me, then I'll leave. Find a couch to crash on."<br />"That should be easy; you can go pack your stuff now."<br />"You haven't heard the rest of the deal. If you can prove to me that you love me, absolutely love me, I'll leave."<br />"Are you fucking kidding me? I would never, ever love a guy like you."<br /><br />So he thinks.... <em>hummmmm... I will constantly sing to her, tell her how much I want to be with her, cook for her and all of her friends, clean up after everybody, buy her jewelry, etc.... buuuuutttt I'm gonna turn the other cheek when she treats me like CAAYYY-RRAAP!</em> He freaking treats her like gold, and she gives NOTHING. Literally NOTHING until like the last 20% of the book, and EVEN THEN, its sketchy and completely unpredictable at best. For me, this sucked the alpha right out of a potentially HAWT alpha hero. He just took her abusive behavior, and did nothing to correct her or at least stand up for himself- it just didn't mesh well with the image that was being set up.<br /><br />Much of her bitchiness is due to trauma from her early teen years (which I won't go into- it's most of the turmoil they deal with), and Hunter brings his fair share baggage along with him as well. So here they are, two damaged people, just trying to find true lurve, while trying to discover the others secrets. Hunter just seems so functional and NORMAL, NICE, SWEET, CARING and LOVING- his trauma (in my honest opinion) is SO much worse than hers, yet he manages to cope, while she manages to let her past have absolute reign in her life. Even after he breaks down and shares all of his secrets- she still withholds secrets, emotion and everyday kindness you would give out to strangers. Unbelievable.<br /><br />The ending left something to be desired- and I pretty much docked it a star because of it. I was literally tapping my screen saying "where's the rest of it??... That was the end??... That sucked!" If there is a sequel coming that I am unaware of, I might reconsider adding a star back- but if not, that ending was not what it could or should have been.<br /><br />The other star I docked was for her just being a pure B. I've never read a book in which the female lead was just SO downright mean. I didn't want to route for her OR for them because of it. It is one thing to be afraid of feelings and try to hide that emotion or avoid, deflect, even throw attitude- it is another to be verbally and/or physically abusive to someone who is trying to love you. <br /><br />They do finally get it together, which is awesome- but in the back of my mind- I'm thinking that if Hunter were one of MY friends, I would have told him to run FAR, FAR away. If Taylor were one of my friends, I would be telling her to THANK HER FREAKING LUCKY STARS that he wants ANYTHING to do her- because she dang sure doesn't deserve him.<br /><br />Important notes: The writing was good- storyline was VERY promising- characters developed well enough (just hated the main character, and really never warmed up to her), disappointing ending which fell flat for me.<br /><br />That is all, friends. (Steps down off of my soapbox)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5960808864979990248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_429220782" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/429220782" />
    <a title="Sofija" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4452470-sofija"><img alt="Sofija" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1287851381p2/4452470.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/429220782?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sofija" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sofija" href="/user/show/4452470-sofija">Sofija</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781478322306" href="/book/show/15748898-my-favorite-mistake">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer429220782" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5185697077128548557">I am a big fan of college romances. Unfortunately, it's very hard to find a good one.<br/><br/>So I was very excited when I found “<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15748898.My_Favorite_Mistake__My_Favorite_Mistake___1_' title='My Favorite Mistake (My Favorite Mistake, #1) by Chelsea M. Cameron' rel='nofollow noopener'>My Favorite Mistake</a>”. New college romance! What can be better? The description reminded me of “<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11505797.Beautiful_Disaster__Beautiful___1_' title='Beautiful Disaster (Beautiful, #1) by Jamie McGuire' rel='nofollow noopener'>Beautiful Disaster</a>”. Boy and girl forced to live together, boy former playboy now trying to win a girl over, girl is having her own reason to stay away from him, they make a bet. You can see similarities. I know that many people don’t like “<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11505797.Beautiful_Disaster__Beautiful___1_' title='Beautiful Disaster (Beautiful, #1) by Jamie McGuire' rel='nofollow noopener'>Beautiful Disaster</a>”, but I loved it so I wa</span>
  <span id="freeText5185697077128548557" style="display:none">I am a big fan of college romances. Unfortunately, it's very hard to find a good one.<br><br>So I was very excited when I found “<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15748898.My_Favorite_Mistake__My_Favorite_Mistake___1_" title="My Favorite Mistake (My Favorite Mistake, #1) by Chelsea M. Cameron" rel="nofollow noopener">My Favorite Mistake</a>”. New college romance! What can be better? The description reminded me of “<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11505797.Beautiful_Disaster__Beautiful___1_" title="Beautiful Disaster (Beautiful, #1) by Jamie McGuire" rel="nofollow noopener">Beautiful Disaster</a>”. Boy and girl forced to live together, boy former playboy now trying to win a girl over, girl is having her own reason to stay away from him, they make a bet. You can see similarities. I know that many people don’t like “<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11505797.Beautiful_Disaster__Beautiful___1_" title="Beautiful Disaster (Beautiful, #1) by Jamie McGuire" rel="nofollow noopener">Beautiful Disaster</a>”, but I loved it so I was happy to read something similar.<br><br>The first thing that rubbed me wrong in “<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15748898.My_Favorite_Mistake__My_Favorite_Mistake___1_" title="My Favorite Mistake (My Favorite Mistake, #1) by Chelsea M. Cameron" rel="nofollow noopener">My Favorite Mistake</a>” was unrealistic of heroes living arrangement. According to the story, Taylor lives in a co-ed dorm. And of course she gets a male roommate. I have trouble believing it. I believe that boys and girls can live in the next rooms. But boy and girl sharing one room? No university would ever support this arrangement. This is just a disaster waiting to happen.<br><br>But I understand that it was necessary for the plot, so I’ll let it go. What I couldn’t understand is why Taylor couldn’t find a way out of this situation. I can suggest her five different solutions that would helped her get rid of Hunter in no time. She so strongly hated this living arrangement, but when girls next door several time offered to switch places with Taylor, she declined. <br><br>And now we got to the main reason why this book didn’t work for me. Taylor. She annoyed me all book long! She has anger management issues. She punched Hunter the first time they met. Then further into the story she beat him senseless when she was having a breakdown. Throughout the book she also threatened to hit his boy-parts. She was yelling at everyone if something was not to her liking. Her roommates were actually scared sometimes to address some issue to her for fear she would explode.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380393538ra/757656.gif" width="245" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She kept accusing Hunter of breaking into her privacy, while she herself secretly studied his phone, eavesdropped on his meetings, and was demanding to open his secret to her. I understand she suffered childhood trauma, but girl<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385283818ra/7117290.gif" width="500" height="282" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Taylor also several times accused Hunter of being bipolar, while it was her behavior that was contradictory. At first, she kisses him with gusto before class, later she doesn’t let him to kiss her in class because she doesn’t want to look like a slut. She chatted with a friend about her night with Hunter, with giving her a few details about their night, later she speaks with her other friend and dodge questions because she “didn’t want to share this special moment with anyone”. <br><br>All in all Taylor was very unpleasant and didn’t deserve Hunter.<br><br>The good thing was that when they actually got together their romance was sweet. I also liked that characters really went to classes and studied. The writing style was tolerable but nothing special. <br><br>I would have enjoyed this book more if there were adequate heroine, but even then it probably would be a mediocre read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5185697077128548557" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/458499512?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isamlq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isamlq" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781478322306" href="/book/show/15748898-my-favorite-mistake">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer458499512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5328653523901454021"><i>"You love me?" </i>he asks her.<br/><i>"No,"</i> she responds<br/><i>"You hate me?"</i> he then asks.<br/><i>"I likely do,"</i> would be <b>me </b>responding in her place.<br/><br/><b>Meh.</b><br/><br/>I mean, truthfully it was fun when it counted; otherwise, it was a <s>bit</s> lot of nothing much. She's sensitive and damaged and has a history she's not dealing with as does the guy. Where she's prickly and tough girl, he's sad sad sad but putting on a front: an ass hole jerkface front that rightfully rubbed her the wrong way the first time they laid eyes on each other. Only</span>
  <span id="freeText5328653523901454021" style="display:none"><i>"You love me?" </i>he asks her.<br /><i>"No,"</i> she responds<br /><i>"You hate me?"</i> he then asks.<br /><i>"I likely do,"</i> would be <b>me </b>responding in her place.<br /><br /><b>Meh.</b><br /><br />I mean, truthfully it was fun when it counted; otherwise, it was a <s>bit</s> lot of nothing much. She's sensitive and damaged and has a history she's not dealing with as does the guy. Where she's prickly and tough girl, he's sad sad sad but putting on a front: an ass hole jerkface front that rightfully rubbed her the wrong way the first time they laid eyes on each other. Only later we find out they can't in fact get enough of each other! It's that last fact that led me to discover that the phrase "eye fucking" can indeed be overused! <br /><br />I didn't get the convoluted bet thing going on. You hate me this happens and you love me that happens. All her denying true feelings then all his running away from his past... I'd have bought it with half that drama cut out of the story, but again my issue of drama. drama. drama surfaced in this one. <br /><br />Bottom line? I didn't really care for this. Oh "New Adult Contemporary Romance," there's nothing "adult" about you... and if all you have is stuff like MY FAVORITE MISTAKE and other stuff like this that I've read so far then should am I just looking forward to more whiny face-this and mopey thought-that, people who talk a good game filled to the brim with angsty me, myself and I moments, and yes, more often than not "edgy" cuss filled (sometimes unnecessarily so) lingo, and too little sense to go around?<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5328653523901454021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12049672382297860308">Cover & Title - 4 out of 5<br/>Favorite Line - “I love you, Missy girl. Even if I can't be with you, know that I'm here. So, that's it. More than the stars, Taylor. More than the stars.” & “Love is simple. You fall and that's it. You'll work the other stuff out. You just gotta let yourself fall and have faith that someone will be there to catch you.” <br/>Favorite Character - Taylor<br/><br/>I thoroughly enjoyed this emotional new adult book, it managed to not only live up to but surpass my expectations. The concep</span>
  <span id="freeText12049672382297860308" style="display:none">Cover &amp; Title - 4 out of 5<br />Favorite Line - “I love you, Missy girl. Even if I can't be with you, know that I'm here. So, that's it. More than the stars, Taylor. More than the stars.” &amp; “Love is simple. You fall and that's it. You'll work the other stuff out. You just gotta let yourself fall and have faith that someone will be there to catch you.” <br />Favorite Character - Taylor<br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed this emotional new adult book, it managed to not only live up to but surpass my expectations. The concept of the story was simple but the content was anything but. <br />Both lead characters back-stories are what make them such awesome characters. The dialog between them is both amusing &amp; sweet. I could "feel" the emotions between them, the love felt <b>so</b> real. <i>"More than the stars"</i> *sign* sometimes it made me so emotionally gooey - like marshmallow fluff.<br />I was so pleased with how everything worked out &amp; the ending was awesome. <br /><br />I would recommend this book &amp; I would read more by this author. </span>

<div id="review_496515617" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/496515617" />
    <a title="Sabrina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8893807-sabrina"><img alt="Sabrina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364503433p2/8893807.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/496515617?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabrina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabrina" href="/user/show/8893807-sabrina">Sabrina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16053437-my-favorite-mistake">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8893807-sabrina?shelf=wtf-just-happened">wtf-just-happened</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8893807-sabrina?shelf=main-character-is-a-bitch">main-character-is-a-bitch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8893807-sabrina?shelf=love-that-fast-really-bleh">love-that-fast-really-bleh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer496515617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8156486691005363652">Honestly, I'm disappointed by the reviews this book got. It had so much potential. I'm a super fast reader and can <s>usually</s> get through a book within a day. This one took 3, just because I kept getting so pissed off. I just wanted it to be over. I wanted to read to the end because I was <b>hoping</b> something would change. Nope. <br/>I'm not going to go through what the book is about because a ton of other people here have said it.<br/>Here are the things that bothered me <u>*May contain spoilers*</u>:<br/><br/>1. So, let me get</span>
  <span id="freeText8156486691005363652" style="display:none">Honestly, I'm disappointed by the reviews this book got. It had so much potential. I'm a super fast reader and can <s>usually</s> get through a book within a day. This one took 3, just because I kept getting so pissed off. I just wanted it to be over. I wanted to read to the end because I was <b>hoping</b> something would change. Nope. <br />I'm not going to go through what the book is about because a ton of other people here have said it.<br />Here are the things that bothered me <u>*May contain spoilers*</u>:<br /><br />1. So, let me get this straight. A hot guy shows up, <b>SHOWS</b> you the papers where they moved him into your apartment and you still have to be a bitch and tell him he can't stay there..<br /><br />2. Punching him. That was the most ridiculous thing I've ever read. Violence is the answer when a guy is just trying to flirt harmlessly. <b>*sarcasm*</b> Then him saying he deserved it. No one, man or female, deserves the shit she put him through. She is the <u>worst</u> character I've ever read about.. EVER. She basically beat him after she got a phone call. She cussed him after her sister call her. I mean really, is that necessary?<br /><br />4. She says she hates him. Then swear to all that is holy, in half a page she is in love and after they do the dirty its all mushy talk.. wtf. Did I just miss 10 pages of them getting along?!?!<br /><br />5. It went from "I hate you" *COLD* to "I love you" *HOT*. Where is the cool-lukewarm-warm stages before it switches that fast. I like reading a book where love developes. How the hell Hunter fell in love with her, well don't ask me.<br /><br /><br /><br />6. I really had a problem with how she thought her problems were worse than his. If I knew a person like her I'd have to shake her and say "a guy TRIED (didn't succeed) to do bad things to you, that boy (aka Hunter) seen his problem with his parents. Actually seen it! You're still alive and so are your parents.. WTF is wrong with you?!?" AGH!<br /><br />I just had so many problems with this book. I think this is the first negative thing I've ever wrote about a book. Mostly because I'm an easy person to please. I just think the author tried to make her a little too strong and a little too psycho for my liking. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8156486691005363652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37372292-danny?shelf=freebies">freebies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37372292-danny?shelf=shes-a-badass">shes-a-badass</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37372292-danny?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37372292-danny?shelf=romantic-drama">romantic-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37372292-danny?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37372292-danny?shelf=college">college</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37372292-danny?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1876912359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5569695687847333550">I've been wanting to read this one for quite some time and imagine my surprise when I found it on my Kindle app while trying to find my next read. Yeah, this is so me... Hahaha<br/><br/>Anyway, I really enjoyed reading this. The writing was really comfortable, it was really smooth to read.<br/>The MC's stories were filled with secrets and tragedies that happened in their past, and some of it still darkened a little of their lives. Their interaction was always funny and good to read, made me laugh and smile wit</span>
  <span id="freeText5569695687847333550" style="display:none">I've been wanting to read this one for quite some time and imagine my surprise when I found it on my Kindle app while trying to find my next read. Yeah, this is so me... Hahaha<br /><br />Anyway, I really enjoyed reading this. The writing was really comfortable, it was really smooth to read.<br />The MC's stories were filled with secrets and tragedies that happened in their past, and some of it still darkened a little of their lives. Their interaction was always funny and good to read, made me laugh and smile with it.<br />Just loved how strong Taylor was. How she 'defended' herself in the beginning, and as Hunter said:<br />"nothing is sexier than a woman who can take care of herself. As far as I'm concerned, the 1950s are over."<br />It's so relieving to read about female characters that are strong and steps up for themselves. And even better is to read about male characters that recognize that strength and are not a chauvinist idiot.<br /><br />There were so parts that annoyed me like when Taylor was trying to find out what Hunter's secrets were about but when he tried to do the same thing, her walls went back up with full force. This is a two-way street. Trust must be earned.<br /><br /><i>"We were both broken, trying to become unbroken. Maybe we just needed a little help. Not to fix each other, but to help us fix ourselves."</i><br /><br />Anyway, I really liked this one. I enjoyed reading it a lot and recommend it to anyone who likes a cute romance with a dark secret looming in the background.<br />It's a great book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5569695687847333550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1698875377196906202"><br/>To me this sounded like it was going to be awesome. But also in my opinion it just missed the mark. <br/><br/>Now the hero in this Hunter was amazing. Him i REALLY liked. sweet, caring, could sing, could cook,had tattoos, easy on the eyes and laughs come easy. <br/><br/>The heroine Taylor just pissed me off. I understand their was some big bad secret (which we found out) as to why she was the way she was. I just didn't see what made her so special in Hunter's eyes. She was just annoying. So that brought the star ra</span>
  <span id="freeText1698875377196906202" style="display:none"><br />To me this sounded like it was going to be awesome. But also in my opinion it just missed the mark. <br /><br />Now the hero in this Hunter was amazing. Him i REALLY liked. sweet, caring, could sing, could cook,had tattoos, easy on the eyes and laughs come easy. <br /><br />The heroine Taylor just pissed me off. I understand their was some big bad secret (which we found out) as to why she was the way she was. I just didn't see what made her so special in Hunter's eyes. She was just annoying. So that brought the star rating down for me. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Oh and that it took 45% for her to finally kiss him and then BAM hands the V card in, after kissing him all of twice..  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> </span>

      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MrEgyJfBtucgjG5/mAPuPcChEpz/fUSGeD/MdT41ECoIl0kaLJ9/j4en2h5v9uTiFv71VDHwyuEjQYrE83bisA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rm6nXvuLEXzEXOO4/OfNVTkv8I8EbyKcG3Na8a7bifKUSM6MQNXYFGN3V9kLEseK73AXR8rirPtADRxAY5h7aA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17630967513138217150">Chelsea M. Cameron is a New York Times/USA Today/Internationally Best Selling author from Maine who now lives and works in Boston. She's a red velvet cake enthusiast, obsessive tea drinker, vegetarian, former cheerleader, and world's worst video gamer. When not writing, she enjoys watching infomercials, getting brunch with her partner, tweeting, and playing fetch with her cat, Sassenach. She has a</span>
  <span id="freeText17630967513138217150" style="display:none">Chelsea M. Cameron is a New York Times/USA Today/Internationally Best Selling author from Maine who now lives and works in Boston. She's a red velvet cake enthusiast, obsessive tea drinker, vegetarian, former cheerleader, and world's worst video gamer. When not writing, she enjoys watching infomercials, getting brunch with her partner, tweeting, and playing fetch with her cat, Sassenach. She has a degree in journalism from the University of Maine, Orono that she promptly abandoned to write about the people in her own head. More often than not, these people turn out to be just as weird as she is.<br /></span>
